According to an arrest statement from the FBI, it\u2019s because an Air National Guardsman named Jack Teixeira posted them online to impress friends.</p> <p>That should scare the hell out of every American and all our allies. This is an intelligence debacle of the first order.</p> <p>It\u2019s a mess, one made messier by the fact that the documents apparently floated around the Internet for months before the U.S. government even noticed.</p> <p>While we wait to hear what Teixeira thought he was doing, let\u2019s consider what all the leaked intelligence tells us about the progress of war in Ukraine. For now, we can put off analyzing the other issues the documents delved into (like the trailer teasing the next Jason Bourne movie).</p> <p>What those documents reveal about the war is, well, not as much as you might expect. This gets to the nature of intelligence reports and summaries.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/politics/pentagon-leak-suspect-searched-leak-classified-network-story-broke-fbi\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>PENTAGON LEAK SUSPECT SEARCHED \u2018LEAK\u2019 ON CLASSIFIED NETWORK AFTER STORY BROKE</strong></a></p> <p>In the movies, intelligence operators supply blinding flashes of truth that propel the plot forward. In real life, strategic intelligence is often ambiguous, contradictory, or just wrong. Think back to the famously wrong assessments of Saddam Hussein\u2019s weapons of mass destruction programs.</p> <p>Intelligence can be accurate, but outdated. That could well be the case with some of these documents.</p> <p>Intelligence can also be malleable. These documents lack a chain-of-custody. They may be subtly doctored or outright manufactured. We don\u2019t know what might have been added, left out or changed from the instant they were leaked. It is still unclear how they proliferated and came to everyone\u2019s attention.</p> <p>In short, any who believes that, by reading these now public documents, they can infer exactly what is going on in Ukraine is making a wild leap of faith. It remains to be seen what can be confirmed.</p> <p>The real question is: How much damage has been done? That, too, remains to be seen. What most freaks out the intelligence community is fear that the information leaked might compromise and endanger valuable sources or enable our foes to identify the methods used to collect it. This could seriously hamper future intelligence collection operations.</p> <p>After a major leak like this, one of the first steps taken\u2014beyond trying to figure out how this happened\u2014is to assess the potential damage risks and then act to mitigate the damage done. These efforts are usually highly classified, so unless that is leaked too, the public may hear very little about what\u2019s been done.</p> <p>If all this seems terribly frustrating, it should. The U.S. government, simply put, ought to do a better job keeping its secrets. Intelligence operations are a constant war of action and counteraction between opposing sides. Only an idiot would assume they would never suffer a damaging intel leak. Good intelligence operations fight like hell to make sure it won\u2019t happen.</p> <p>This leak is well beyond an embarrassment. It undermines our friends\u2019 and allies\u2019 confidence in the competence of our Defense Department. It may lead to operational failures and might even get people killed.</p> <p>This should serve as a harsh<a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/politics/defense/pentagon\" target=\"_blank\"> reminder to the Pentagon</a> that our national security is Job One. Some people think the armed forces should be used to fight global warming, or advance DEI, or manufacture excuses for the failures of the Afghan withdrawal. But national defense is not about advancing political agendas.</p> <p>Further, the nature of these leaks are particularly disturbing. This was not an adversary coming after us. This was one of us doing something incredibly reckless.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/newsletters\" target=\"_blank\"><strong><u>CLICK HERE TO GET THE OPINION NEWSLETTER</u></strong></a></p> <p>To be honest, this is exactly the kind of selfish, self-absorbed, immature behavior we can expect from certain members of Generation Z. That said, we don\u2019t expect young people that join the military to act that way, or think the military is there to empower or encourage that kind of behavior.</p> <p>Again, it goes back to asking what the heck is the military doing recruiting and retaining people like Jack Teixeira, or Chelsea Manning, another notorious leaker in uniform, or hiring contractors like the infamous Edward Snowden?</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/politics/defense\" target=\"_blank\">Defense officials</a> can beat their chests all they want, saying how seriously they take this incident and how seriously they take the task of defending America\u2019s interests. But when you look at the state of today\u2019s Pentagon, it\u2019s hard not to ask: Do we really believe them?</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/person/c/james-jay-carafano\" "https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2023/04/931/524/Little-Hometown_Family-Shot_option-2-1.jpg?ve=1&tl=1", "Health", "https://moxie.foxnews.com/google-publisher/health.xml"], ["https://www.foxnews.com/health/weight-loss-older-adults-associated-risk-death", "Weight loss in older adults associated with risk of death, study shows", "<p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/nutrition-and-fitness/weight-loss\" target=\"_blank\">Weight loss in older adults</a> may increase their risk of death, according to new research.\u00a0</p> <p>A cohort study published in the journal JAMA Network Open Monday looked at more than 16,000 adults in <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/world/world-regions/australia\" target=\"_blank\">the U.S. and Australia</a>.</p> <p>The authors from the University of Melbourne, Monash University and others said weight loss in healthy older individuals was found to be associated with an increased risk of cancer, cardiovascular disease and \"other life-limiting conditions.\"\u00a0</p> <p>\"Physicians should be aware of the significance of weight loss, especially among older men,\" it said.\u00a0</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/health/weight-loss-medications-ozempic-wegovy-what-know-before-stop-taking-them\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>WEIGHT LOSS MEDICATIONS OZEMPIC AND WEGOVY: WHAT TO KNOW BEFORE YOU STOP TAKING THEM</strong></a></p> <p>Study participants, recruited between March 2010 and December 2014, were <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/world/world-regions/australia\" target=\"_blank\">70 years and older in Australia</a> and 65 years and older in the U.S.\u00a0</p> <p>Data analysis was performed from April 2022 to September 2022.</p> <p>The adults were weighed annually, with researchers warning physicians to be aware of the \"significant association\" between relatively minor weight loss of more than 5% and mortality.\u00a0</p> <p>Older men who lost between 5%-10% of weight \u2014 compared to those who had stable weight \u2014 had a 33% higher risk of mortality, and those who lost more than 10% of weight had a 289% higher chance of mortality.</p> <p>Women who lost between 5%-10% of their weight had a 26% higher chance of mortality, and those who lost more than 10% had a 114% higher chance.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/tech/5-best-telemedicine-apps-virtual-health-care\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>5 BEST TELEMEDICINE APPS FOR VIRTUAL HEALTH CARE</strong></a></p> <p>The authors posited that the observation that weight loss was associated with mortality among men may be the result of the different body composition characteristics of men and women.</p> <p>For example, men have a higher percentage of body muscle than body fat compared to women.</p> <p>They said that a \"likely\" explanation for the findings is that weight loss can be an early premonitory indicator of the presence of various <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/entertainment/events/illness\" target=\"_blank\">life-shortening diseases</a>, noting that weight loss in this age group was largely associated with a reduction of appetite.</p> <p>Those who gained weight did not show an increased risk of mortality in the group.</p> <p>\"Further research will be needed to determine more precisely the association between weight loss and <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/health\" target=\"_blank\">the onset of fatal diseases</a> and whether clinical or laboratory investigations can identify individuals for whom early intervention may be effective,\" it said.</p>", "Tue, 11 Apr 2023 15:44:21 EDT", "https://a57.foxnews.com/static.foxnews.com/foxnews.com/content/uploads/2023/04/931/523/man-weight-tape-measure.jpg?ve=1&tl=1", "Health", "https://moxie.foxnews.com/google-publisher/health.xml"], ["https://www.foxnews.com/health/adhd-numbers-climbing-dramatically-us-especially-among-women-says-study", "ADHD numbers climbing dramatically in the U.S., especially among women, says new study", "<p>The number of people diagnosed with <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/education/adhd\"><u>attention-deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD)</u></a> is climbing steadily in the U.S. \u2014 especially among women, a new study found.</p> <p>While cases have risen across all age groups, the spike has been most significant among women.\u00a0</p> <p>The share of females between the ages of 23 and 49 years of age diagnosed with the disorder nearly doubled from 2020 to 2022.</p> <p>To reach these findings, investigators from Epic Research, a health analytics firm based in <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/us/us-regions/midwest/wisconsin\" target=\"_blank\">Verona, Wisconsin</a>, analyzed data from 3,389,383 patients who were diagnosed with ADHD between 2010 and 2022.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/health/sniffing-body-odor-sweat-reduce-social-anxiety-research-suggests\"><strong><u>SNIFFING BODY ODOR FROM SWEAT COULD REDUCE SOCIAL ANXIETY, NEW RESEARCH SUGGESTS</u></strong></a></p> <p>Since 2010, the rates of ADHD have tripled overall, the study found \u2014 but the share of patients taking <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/healthy-living/medications\" target=\"_blank\">prescribed medications</a> for the disorder has remained consistent.</p> <p>Males have historically been more likely to be diagnosed with ADHD, but the study findings indicated that the gender gap has been closing over the past 12 years.</p> <p>\"The ratio of males to females diagnosed with ADHD decreased nearly five-fold during that time, from males being 133% more likely to be diagnosed with ADHD than females in 2010 to 28% more likely to be diagnosed with ADHD in 2022,\" Epic Research stated in a discussion of the study findings.\u00a0</p> <p>Previous studies have shown that <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/healthy-living/womens-health\"><u>females with ADHD</u></a> tend to have very different symptoms than males \u2014 which could prevent them from getting evaluated and diagnosed.</p> <p>\"Data for ADHD tends to skew heavily toward school-age males,\" Dr. Joseph Galasso, a psychologist at Baker Street Behavioral Health <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/us/us-regions/northeast/new-jersey\"><u>in New Jersey</u></a>, told Fox News Digital in a phone interview. He was not involved in the new study.</p> <p>\"Boys tend to be more active, with overt behaviors that lead to earlier diagnoses.\"</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/health/seasonal-affective-disorder-causes-symptoms-seek-help\"><strong><u>SEASONAL AFFECTIVE DISORDER SYMPTOMS, CAUSES AND WHEN TO SEEK HELP FOR MOOD DISORDER</u></strong></a></p> <p>On the other hand, he said girls tend to \"fly under the radar,\" as their symptoms tend to be internalized.</p> <p>Instead of hyperactivity, ADHD can look <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/mental-health/depression\" target=\"_blank\">more like depression</a> or anxiety in females, he added.</p> <p>Overall, women tend to receive ADHD diagnoses later in life, often during their 30s or 40s, as WebMD reported.</p> <p>This doesn\u2019t surprise Dr. Galasso, who pointed out that the many stressors and demands of adult life could compel women to seek help.\u00a0</p> <p>\"As women begin careers, <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/lifestyle/parenting\" target=\"_blank\">have children</a> and juggle other pressures, it may become harder to maintain life with ADHD,\" he said.\u00a0</p> <p>Additionally, ADHD may have been confused with other <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/mental-health\"><u>mental health challenges</u></a>, resulting in many cases going undiagnosed until later in life.</p> <p>\"They may come to realize that it hasn\u2019t just been <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/mental-health/stress-and-anxiety\"><u>stress or anxiety</u></a> they\u2019ve been dealing with,\" said Dr. Galasso.\u00a0</p> <p>Another factor that could contribute to the increase is that it\u2019s easier to access a psychiatrist or psychologist to receive care, he said.\u00a0</p> <p>Also, patients have become more informed about the disorder overall.\u00a0</p> <p>\"I have patients who come to my practice and have pretty much already diagnosed themselves,\" the doctor said.\u00a0</p> <p>\"They might have trouble concentrating at work, have memory problems or struggle to focus, or are just really stressed out. And they\u2019ve done their research and have an idea that it could be ADHD.\"</p> <p>Dr. Jackie Gerhart, chief medical officer at Epic and a family medicine physician based in Wisconsin, said that in future studies, she would like to look at the mode of delivery of ADHD services \u2014 specifically, whether telehealth is associated with the number of new ADHD diagnoses and the share of patients who were prescribed medication.\u00a0</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/newsletters?cmpid=fnfirstnl\"><strong><u>CLICK HERE TO SIGN UP FOR OUR HEALTH NEWSLETTER</u></strong></a></p> <p>\"Telehealth helps increase access to mental health care, so it\u2019s possible that patients who didn\u2019t previously have a diagnosis of ADHD were able to receive the diagnosis and care through expanded telehealth access,\" she told Fox News Digital.\u00a0</p> <p>\"It would be interesting to study whether telehealth services are used differently by male or female patients,\" she added.</p>
